J.">21</a>, <a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0040_R_d65608047e1727" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - J. Mater. Chem. A">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> resulting in a shift in the position of the oxidation and reduction peaks. In addition, at higher scanning rates, the pseudocapacitive behavior becomes more pronounced and will serve as the dominant sodium storage behavior, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0003">3g</a>. At 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, the pseudocapacitive contribution is only 50.3%, while at 20&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, the pseudocapacitive contribution has already reached 92.8%. In other words, the capacity contributed by the redox reaction is only 7.2%, which will inevitably lead to a significant decrease in the intensity of the redox peaks, even the disappearance of part of the redox peaks.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0010_R_d65608047e1740" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Chem. Eng. J.">10</a>, <a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0021_R_d65608047e1740" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Chem. Eng. J.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The in situ magnetometry (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5c–e</a>) is used to explore the reaction mechanism for the FeS/C@Na cells through quantifying the magnetization variation upon voltage change recoreded by testing CV curves (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5b</a>). Through monitoring magnetization and voltage at 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, it can be seen that the magnetization is basically unchanged from open circuit voltage to 1&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5c</a>), indicating that the intercalation reaction does not obviously change magnetization of electrode. The magnetization rapidly increases when discharge to ≈1&nbsp;V, reaching a maximum value at ∼ 0.45&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5c</a>). The voltage values fall within the voltage range that the conversion reaction occurs. Thus, the rapid increase of magnetization is ascribed to the formation of superparamagnetic Fe nanoparticles during conversion reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0041_R_d65608047e1760" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Nat. Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0042_R_d65608047e1760" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - ACS Energy Lett.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Following discharge from 0.45 to 0.01&nbsp;V, the magnetization represents a decreased trend (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5c</a>). The specific reasons are discussed below.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0041_R_d65608047e1769" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Nat. Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Once superparamagnetic Fe nanoparticles are formed, which would induce the injection of spin-polarized electrons into their not-full d-orbits under the magnetic field. For 3d transition metals, the different filling of spin-up and spin-down d bands can lead to different ferromagnetism, in which the spin-up d bands are filled much more than the spin-down d bands. The net magnetization can be calculated based on the equation that <i>M</i> = (<i>N↑</i>-<i>N↓</i>)*<i>µ<sub>B</sub></i>, in which N↑ and N↓ are number of electrons for spin up and spin down, respectively, and <i>µ<sub>B</sub></i> is the Bohr magneton. Owing to the dominant population of spin-minority states near the Fermi level on the surface of 3d ferromagnetic metals, the spin-polarized electrons are more inclined to inject into spin-down d bands than spin-up d bands, resulting in a decrease of the value of N↑-N↓, thus causing the decrease of the magnetization. The accumulation of spin-polarized electrons on the surface and inside of Fe induces the movement toward Fe of sodium ions and makes sodium ions accumulate on the surface of Fe under electric field, resulting in spin-polarized surface capacitance and the construction of a space charge region, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5f</a>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0041_R_d65608047e1792" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Nat. Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> When charged from 0.01 to ≈1&nbsp;V, the magnetization represents a gradually increased trend due to removal of spin-polarized electrons from Fe. When charge from 1 to ≈2.2&nbsp;V, the magnetization decreases rapidly due to the oxidation of Fe into Na<sub>x</sub>FeS and FeS. In subsequent cycles, the shape of the magnetic spectra remains unchanged with the first cycle, suggesting that the magnetic responses versus the electrode voltage are highly reversible (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5c</a>). Based on the above results, spin-polarized electron injection and extraction in Fe occur between 0.01 and 1&nbsp;V; thus, the magnetic response versus the electrode voltage from 0.01 to 1&nbsp;V at 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> is tested (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5d</a>). The magnetization gradually decreases in the discharging process from 1 to 0.01&nbsp;V and increases anew in the charging process from 0.01 to 1&nbsp;V, which proves high reversibility of capacitive-like surface reaction that involves superparamagnetic Fe.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0041_R_d65608047e1808" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Nat. Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0043_R_d65608047e1808" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Matter">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To demonstrate magnetic response rate, the magnetic spectra are tested at a high scanning rate of 20&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5e</a>). The magnetization shows a similar change trend to that tested at 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, which demonstrates that the capacitive-like surface reaction that involves superparamagnetic Fe exists and is highly reversible under ultrafast rate (time of 50 s per discharge or charge) of spin-polarized electrons injection and extraction. The observed electrochemical, structural, and magnetic evolution of the FeS/C electrodes demonstrate that the extra sodium ion storage capacity (the reversible capacity (664.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) of FeS/C exceeds the theoretical capacity (609 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) of FeS) arises from spin-polarized surface capacitance of superparamagnetic Fe nanoparticles, which also can boost stable and fast sodium ion transport, thus ensuring high capacity, excellent cycling stability, and outstanding fast-charging capability of FeS/C electrodes. To further explore the dynamic behavior of the FeS/C electrodes between 0.01 and 1&nbsp;V, the CV curves are tested from 0.1 to 20&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5g</a>) and the enlarged CV curves from 0.1 to 2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Supporting Information). From Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5h</a>, the b value is approximately equal to 1, which fully proves a complete capacitive-controlled process at 0.01–1&nbsp;V voltages with ≈100% capacitive contribution at various scanning rates (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5i</a>). In order to further testify the influence of spin-polarized surface capacitance of superparamagnetic Fe nanoparticles on ion transport and storage, the cycling stability is tested from 0.01 to 1&nbsp;V at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Before testing, the electrode is activated at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.01-3&nbsp;V voltage ranges in the first three cycles. The FeS/C electrode shows a high capacity of 189.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a high capacity retention of 96.8% after 10&nbsp;000 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5j</a>), proving that spin-polarized surface capacitance of superparamagnetic Fe nanoparticles can ensure stable and fast sodium ion transport. The capacity of 189.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> retains 63.1% of the capacity obtained at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> at voltage ranges of 0.01–3&nbsp;V after 10&nbsp;000 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0003">3j</a>), in which the capacity does not show an obvious fade in first few hundred cycles. However, the FeS/C electrode shows rapid capacity fade from 1 to 500 cycles at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> at voltage ranges of 0.01–3&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0003">3j</a>). The results indicate that spin-polarized surface capacitance of superparamagnetic Fe is dominant in stable ion transport and storage at high current density. Besides, from GITT curve (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information), the D<sub>Na+</sub> from the cut-off voltage (≈0.45&nbsp;V) of the conversion reaction to 0.01&nbsp;V and the starting voltage (≈1&nbsp;V) of the oxidation reaction to 0.01&nbsp;V are much higher than those voltage ranges from the starting voltage (≈1&nbsp;V) of the conversion reaction to its cut-off voltage and from the starting voltage of the oxidation reaction to its cut-off voltage (≈2.2&nbsp;V). The result further indicates that spin-polarized surface capacitance of superparamagnetic Fe is favorable for fast ion transport.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400246-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/b5ea73d2-78e4-4320-bb79-989603a8e313/aenm202400246-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/b5ea73d2-78e4-4320-bb79-989603a8e313/aenm202400246-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4007af0d-4fbb-4dd2-9235-0748d4d3eea8/aenm202400246-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/b5ea73d2-78e4-4320-bb79-989603a8e313/aenm202400246-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400246-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400246" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Ex situ XRD patterns, b) CV curves at 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, c–e) In situ magnetometry characterizations: c) at voltage windows of 0.01-3&nbsp;V with a scanning rate of 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, d) at voltage windows of 0.01-1&nbsp;V with a scanning rate of 0.5&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, e) at voltage windows of 0.01–1&nbsp;V with a scanning rate of 20&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. f) Schematic diagram of formation of space charge zone. g–i) Kinetic analysis of FeS/C at voltage windows of 0.01–1 V: g) CV curves at different scanning rates, h) Logip versus Logv, and i) pseudocapacitive contribution percentages. j) Cycling curve of FeS/C at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> between 0.01 and 1&nbsp;V.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Based on the above results, it can be concluded that our work brings much knowledge to the understanding of the FeS electrode for SIBs. First, this work confirms the effectiveness of the vapor-pressure-induced synthesis route for the preparation of micro-sized single-crystal FeS/C yolk-shell structure, which can act as a new synthesis strategy for other transition-metal based SIB anodes. Second, this work demonstrates the effectiveness of the micro-sized single-crystal sheets for improving transport and storage of sodium ions, which provides a guide for the design of other fast-charging transition-metal-based SIB anodes along with high capacity. Third, superior fast-charging performances and unprecedented cycling life over 10&nbsp;000 cycles make FeS/C composites promising applications in SIBs. This can advance SIBs in the application progress of high-speed EVs and LSESS. Last, the fast sodium storage mechanism during the conversion reaction and subsequent ion storage has been revealed. This work in-depthly demonstrates the mechanism of stable and fast ion transport in FeS/C electrodes by using innovative tools such as in situ magnetometry and in situ TEM, along with testing electrochemical performances at different voltage ranges. It is found that the spin-polarized surface capacitance effect can ensure fast ion transport stably, which provides a deep understanding on enhancement of cycling stability and rate performances for 3d transition-metal-based conversion-type SIB anodes. This is the first time strong “spin-polarized surface capacitance” has been observed in transition-metal sulfides in SIBs, which provides extra capacity beyond the theoretical value and boosts ion transport stably.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202400246-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202400246-sec-0060-title">2.4 Electrochemical Performances Characterizations in Full Cells</h3>
            
            <p>To assess the practical application potential of FeS/C anode, the full cells are assembled using Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as cathode and tested at a voltage window of 1.0 to 3.5&nbsp;V. Before assembling, the FeS/C anodes are pre-cycled for three cycles to enhance its first CE in half cells. The charge/discharge curves show a similar shape to testify good reversibility of electrodes during 1–100 cycling at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6a</a>). After 100 cycles, a high capacity of 645.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> is delivered with 96.8% capacity retention (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6b</a>). To demonstrate the origin of high capacity (645.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) in full cells, the FeS/C electrode was observed by TEM when the full cell was charged to 3.0&nbsp;V. As observed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information), vast superparamagnetic Fe nanocrystals (≈3&nbsp;nm) appear, indicating that the conversion reaction has been completed at the potential. When charging from 3.0 to 3.5&nbsp;V, the full cell shows extra capacity arising from the contribution of spin-polarized surface capacitance at the interfaces of Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S, as confirmed by in situ magnetometry (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0005">5c–f</a>). At 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the full cell obtains a capacity of 494.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a high capacity retention of 87.7% after 500 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6c</a>). The rate curve (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6d</a>) shows that the full cell has capacities of 665.3, 627.2, 593.9, 566.6, 520.8, and 469.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05, 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, and 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Remarkably, the capacity anew returns to pristine value when again back to 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> to indicate high reversibility of electrode during rate test. The energy density of the full cells can be calculated based on the equation that gravimetric energy density (<i>E</i><sub>G</sub>, Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>) = C*V/m<sub>active</sub>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0044_R_d65608047e1969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J. Energy Storage">44</a>, <a href="#aenm202400246-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202400246-bib-0045_R_d65608047e1969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Carbon">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> in which C represents the cell capacity (0.66 mAh), V indicates the nominal voltage (2.075&nbsp;V), and m<sub>active</sub> is the total active mass of cathode (1.13&nbsp;mg) and anode (6.40&nbsp;mg). Therefore, the E<sub>G</sub> is calculated as 181.9&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>. The relationship between E<sub>G</sub> and charge time is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6e</a>. It can be seen that a E<sub>G</sub> of 128.2&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> is obtained at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> with a short charge time of 14.1&nbsp;min and retains 70.5% energy density obtained at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, which fully indicates that the full cell has excellent fast-charging capability. A single full cell can power 65 light-emitting diode (LED) arrays (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6f</a>). Prominently, at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> the full cell can cycle over 1000 times with a capacity of 334.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and a high capacity retention of 71.9% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6g</a>). Obviously, at similar or same current densities, the CE of full cells is more stable than those in half cells, indicating that FeS/C electrodes have better compatibility with Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode electrodes than sodium metal. This may be due to the uneven surface of the sodium metal caused by the process of making sodium blocks into sodium sheets. Clearly, the full cells show excellent electrochemical performances, which is ascribed to good rate performance and stability of the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information) and FeS/C anode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0003">3</a>). The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode exhibits a high capacity of 112.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles with a capacity retention of 97.5% at 0.1 C (1 C = 117&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>), a high capacity of 87.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 90.4% after 2000 cycles at 5 C, and 92.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information). In full cells, the current density of 5 C for the cathode is approximately equivalent to the current density of 3.3 A g<sup>−1</sup> for the anode due to the difference in mass loading between the cathode and anode. Generally speaking, the electrochemical performances of the full cells are related to the electrochemical performances of the cathode and anode in half cells, both of which will affect the final performances of the full cells. Among the two, the electrochemical performances of the full cells are closer to the one with poorer electrochemical performances. The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode exhibits better rate performance and stability than the FeS/C anode. Therefore, the rate performance and stability of the full cells are greatly affected by the anode instead of the cathode in this work. Clearly, the cycling and rate performances of the full cells are worse than those of the anode in half cells, which may be due to the sodium excess in the half cells (sodium metal as counter/reference electrode), which can improve cycle stability and rate performance. To indicate the advantages of our synthesized FeS/C anodes, the capacity, cycling stability, and fast-charging performance of our full cells are compared with previously reported full cells when FeS-based composites as anodes by plotting a 3D diagram (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202400246-fig-0006">6h</a>), in which the x-axis, y-axis, and z-axis represent the current density, cycle number, and capacity, respectively, and the corresponding data are summarized in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). Clearly, whether at low (0.05 and 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>) or high (2 A g<sup>−1</sup>) current densities, our full cells exhibit the highest capacity after cycling (points 1, 2, and 4). Significantly, the cycle number can reach 500 and 1000 at current densities of 0.5 and 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> (points 2 and 4), respectively, which are also significantly higher than the reported FeS-based full cells. Furthermore, regarding fast-charging performance, our full cell achieves the highest capacity (469.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> (point 3). Consequently, the fast-charging and cycling performances of our full cells are superior to the previous reports. The high energy density and excellent fast-charging and cycling performances of our full cells indicate the good application promising of FeS/C anodes in SIBs.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202400246-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7045a57a-75ec-4802-85e3-ea0bb94c73fd/aenm202400246-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/7045a57a-75ec-4802-85e3-ea0bb94c73fd/aenm202400246-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5388a94e-db13-4ca5-a1dd-7e0bdcabb648/aenm202400246-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7045a57a-75ec-4802-85e3-ea0bb94c73fd/aenm202400246-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202400246-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202400246" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Full-cell performance characterizations: a) Galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, b) Cycling curve at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, c) Cycling curve at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, d) Rate performance, e) Relationship of E<sub>G</sub> and charge time, f) The powered LED arrays, g) Cycling curve at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and h) Performance comparison of reported full cells composing of FeS-based anodes with our full cell.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202400246-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202400246-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>To conclude, we synthesize a FeS/C yolk-shell structure via a vapor-pressure induced synthesis route that ultrathin carbon layers coat on the surface of FeS nanosheets with a hollow space between the two, which, together with carbon layers, can greatly alleviate volume expansion of FeS during sodiation. Furthermore, the carbon coating layers can greatly enhance electrical conductivity of FeS, thus boosting charge transport. In situ TEM observation confirms an ultralow size change of 4.0% in FeS/C nanosheets and the formation of ultrasmall Fe nanoparticles (≈3&nbsp;nm) after full sodiation. In situ magnetometry reveals spin-polarized electrons induced evolution of electrode magnetization and demonstrates the existence of spin-polarized surface capacitance at Fe/Na<sub>2</sub>S interfaces, which can boost stable and fast ion transport, and increase extra sodium ion storage capacity between 0.01 and 1&nbsp;V, especially at high current density. As a result, the FeS/C nanosheets deliver a high reversible capacity of 664.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> and 300.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 10&nbsp;000 cycles at 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 81.1% at a voltage range of 0.01-3&nbsp;V in half cells, which is best among previous reports on FeS-based sodium-ion-battery anodes. In addition, the assembled full cells can deliver a high energy density of 181.9&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> and remain 70.5% at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Remarkably, the full cells also exhibit stable and fast electrochemical performance with capacity retention of 71.9% obtained after 1000 cycles at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, which is superior to all the reported full cells when FeS-based composites as anodes. This work confirms the effectiveness of the vapor-pressure-induced synthesis route for the preparation high-performance FeS/C SIB anodes, which can act as a new synthesis strategy for other transition-metal-based SIB anodes. Besides, this work also demonstrates the effectiveness of spin-polarized surface capacitance effect on boosting stable and fast ion transport, which provides a deep understanding of the enhancement of cycling stability and rate performances for 3d transition-metal-based conversion-type SIB anodes.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
